3166-2:PY">PY</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Country_code_top-level_domain" title="Country code top-level domain">Internet TLD</a></th><td><a href="/wiki/.py" title=".py">.py</a></td></tr><tr><td colspan="2" style="text-align:center"><div style="text-align:left;margin-left:auto; margin-right:auto;"><ol style="list-style-type: lower-alpha; margin-left: 1em; font-size:90%;">\n<li value="1">Mixed European and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Amerindian" title="Amerindian">Amerindian</a>.</li>\n</ol></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><b>Paraguay</b> (<span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/&#712;/: primary stress follows">&#712;</span><span title="\'p\' in \'pie\'">p</span><span title="/&#230;r/: \'arr\' in \'marry\'">&#230;r</span><span title="/&#601;/: \'a\' in \'about\'">&#601;</span><span title="/&#609;/: \'g\' in \'guy\'">&#609;</span><span title="\'w\' in \'wind\'">w</span><span title="/a&#618;/: \'i\' in \'tide\'">a&#618;</span></span>/</a></span></span>; <small>Spanish pronunciation:&#160;</small><span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Spanish" title="Help:IPA/Spanish">[pa&#638;a&#712;&#611;waj]</a></span>; <a href="/wiki/Guarani_language" title="Guarani language">Guarani</a>: <i lang="gn">Paragu&#225;i</i>, <small></small><span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA" title="Help:IPA">[pa&#638;a&#712;&#624;waj]</a></span>), officially the <b>Republic of Paraguay</b> (Spanish: <i lang="es">Rep&#250;blica del Paraguay</i>; Guarani: <i lang="gn">Tet&#227; Paragu&#225;i</i>), is one of only two <a href="/wiki/Landlocked_country" title="Landlocked country">landlocked countries</a> in <a href="/wiki/South_America" title="South America">South America</a> (the other is <a href="/wiki/Bolivia" title="Bolivia">Bolivia</a>). It is bordered by <a href="/wiki/Argentina" title="Argentina">Argentina</a> to the south and southwest, <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a> to the east and northeast, and Bolivia to the northwest. Paraguay lies on both banks of the <a href="/wiki/Paraguay_River" title="Paraguay River">Paraguay River</a>, which runs through the center of the country from north to south. Due to its central location in South America, it is sometimes referred to as <i>Coraz&#243;n de Sudam&#233;rica</i> ("Heart of South America").<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[9]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Spanish <a href="/wiki/Conquistador" title="Conquistador">conquistadores</a> arrived in 1524 after navigating northwards from the <a href="/wiki/R%C3%ADo_de_la_Plata" title="R&#237;o de la Plata">R&#237;o de la Plata</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Paran%C3%A1_River" title="Paran&#225; River">Paran&#225; River</a>, and finally up the <a href="/wiki/Paraguay_River" title="Paraguay River">Paraguay River</a>. In 1537, they established the city of <a href="/wiki/Asunci%C3%B3n" title="Asunci&#243;n">Asunci&#243;n</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[10]</a></sup> which was the first capital of the <a href="/wiki/Governorate_of_the_R%C3%ADo_de_la_Plata" title="Governorate of the R&#237;o de la Plata">Governorate of Paraguay and R&#237;o de la Plata</a>. Paraguay was the epicenter of the <a href="/wiki/Reductions" title="Reductions">Jesuit Missions</a>, where the <a href="/wiki/Guaran%C3%AD_people" title="Guaran&#237; people">Guaran&#237; people</a> were educated and introduced to <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christianity</a> and European culture under the direction of the <a href="/wiki/Society_of_Jesus" title="Society of Jesus">Society of Jesus</a> in <a href="/wiki/Jesuit_reduction" title="Jesuit reduction">Jesuit reductions</a>, mainly during the 17th century.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[11]</a></sup> However, after the <a href="/wiki/Suppression_of_the_Society_of_Jesus" title="Suppression of the Society of Jesus">expulsion of the Jesuits</a> from Spanish territories in 1767, Paraguay increasingly became a peripheral colony, with few urban centers and settlers. Following <a href="/wiki/Independence_of_Paraguay" title="Independence of Paraguay">independence from Spain</a> at the beginning of the 19th century, Paraguay was ruled by a series of <a href="/wiki/Authoritarianism" title="Authoritarianism">authoritarian</a> governments who generally implemented <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nationalist" title="Nationalist">nationalist</a>, <a href="/wiki/Isolationism" title="Isolationism">isolationist</a> and <a href="/wiki/Protectionism" title="Protectionism">protectionist</a> policies. This period ended with the disastrous <a href="/wiki/Paraguayan_War" title="Paraguayan War">Paraguayan War</a>, during which Paraguay lost at least 50% of its prewar population and around 25&#8211;33% of its territory to the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_the_Triple_Alliance" title="Treaty of the Triple Alliance">Triple Alliance</a> of <a href="/wiki/Argentina" title="Argentina">Argentina</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a> and <a href="/wiki/Uruguay" title="Uruguay">Uruguay</a>. In the 20th century, Paraguay faced another major international conflict &#8211; the <a href="/wiki/Chaco_War" title="Chaco War">Chaco War</a> &#8211; against Bolivia, from which the Paraguayans emerged victorious. Afterwards, the country entered a period of military dictatorships, ending with the 35 year regime of <a href="/wiki/Alfredo_Stroessner" title="Alfredo Stroessner">Alfredo Stroessner</a> that lasted until he was toppled in 1989 by an internal military coup. This marked the beginning of the "democratic era" of Paraguay.\n</p><p>With around 7 million inhabitants, Paraguay is a founding member of <a href="/wiki/Mercosur" title="Mercosur">Mercosur</a>, an original member of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Organization_of_American_States" title="Organization of American States">Organization of American States</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Non-Aligned_Movement" title="Non-Aligned Movement">Non-Aligned Movement</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Lima_Group" title="Lima Group">Lima Group</a>. Also, the city of <a href="/wiki/Luque" title="Luque">Luque</a>, in Asuncion\'s Metropolitan Area, is the seat of the <a href="/wiki/CONMEBOL" title="CONMEBOL">CONMEBOL</a>. The Guarani culture is very influential and more than 90% of the people speak different forms of the Guarani language. Paraguayans are known for being a very happy and easy-living people and many times the country topped the "world\'s happiest place" charts because of the "positive experiences" lived and expressed by the population.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[12]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[13]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="toc" History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Paraguay" title="History of Paraguay">History of Paraguay</a></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Pre-Columbian_Era">Pre-Columbian Era</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Paraguay&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Pre-Columbian Era">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Indigenous_people" title="Indigenous people">indigenous</a> <a href="/wiki/Guaran%C3%AD_people" title="Guaran&#237; people">Guaran&#237;</a> had been living in eastern Paraguay for at least a millennium before the arrival of the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Empire" title="Spanish Empire">Spanish</a>. Western Paraguay, the <a href="/wiki/Gran_Chaco" title="Gran Chaco">Gran Chaco</a>, was inhabited by nomads of whom the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Guaycuru" title="Guaycuru">Guaycuru</a> peoples were the most prominent. The Paraguay River was roughly the dividing line between the agricultural Guarani people to the east and the nomadic and semi-nomadic people to the west in the Gran Chaco. The Guarcuru nomads were known for their warrior traditions and were not fully pacified until the late 19th century. These indigenous tribes belonged to five distinct language families, which were the bases of their major divisions. Differing language speaking groups were generally competitive over resources and territories. They were further divided into tribes by speaking languages in branches of these families. Today 17 separate <a href="/wiki/Ethnolinguistics" title="Ethnolinguistics">ethnolinguistic</a> groups remain.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Colonization">Colonization</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Paraguay&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Colonization">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The first Europeans in the area were Spanish explorers in 1516.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-eec_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-eec-16">[14]</a></sup> The Spanish explorer <a href="/wiki/Juan_de_Salazar_de_Espinosa" title="Juan de Salazar de Espinosa">Juan de Salazar de Espinosa</a> founded the settlement of <a href="/wiki/Asunci%C3%B3n" title="Asunci&#243;n">Asunci&#243;n</a> on 15 August 1537. The city eventually became the center of a <a href="/wiki/Spanish_colonization_of_the_Americas" title="Spanish colonization of the Americas">Spanish colonial province of Paraguay</a>.\n</p><p>An attempt to create an autonomous Christian Indian nation <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cite_wdl|#2581_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-cite_wdl|#2581-17">[15]</a></sup> was undertaken by <a href="/wiki/Society_of_Jesus" title="Society of Jesus">Jesuit</a> missions and settlements in this part of South America in the eighteenth century, which included portions of Uruguay, Argentina, and Brazil. They developed <a href="/wiki/Jesuit_reduction" title="Jesuit reduction">Jesuit reductions</a> to bring Guarani populations together at Spanish missions and protect them from virtual slavery by Spanish settlers and Portuguese slave raiders, the <a href="/wiki/Bandeirantes" title="Bandeirantes">Bandeirantes</a>. In addition to seeking their conversion to Christianity. Catholicism in Paraguay was influenced by the indigenous peoples; the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Syncretic" title="Syncretic">syncretic</a> religion has absorbed native elements. The <i>reducciones</i> flourished in eastern Paraguay for about 150 years, until the expulsion of the Jesuits by the Spanish Crown in 1767. The ruins of two 18th-century <a href="/wiki/Jesuit_Missions_of_La_Sant%C3%ADsima_Trinidad_de_Paran%C3%A1_and_Jes%C3%BAs_de_Tavarangue" title="Jesuit Missions of La Sant&#237;sima Trinidad de Paran&#225; and Jes&#250;s de Tavarangue">Jesuit Missions of La Sant&#237;sima Trinidad de Paran&#225; and Jes&#250;s de Tavarangue</a> have been designated as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Sites" title="World Heritage Sites">World Heritage Sites</a> by <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cite_wdl|#2581_17-1"><a href="#cite_note-cite_wdl|#2581-17">[15]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In western Paraguay Spanish settlement and Christianity were strongly resisted by the nomadic Guaycuru and other nomads from the 16th century onward. Most of these peoples were absorbed into the <a href="/wiki/Mestizo" title="Mestizo">mestizo</a> population in the 18th and 19th centuries.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Independence_and_rule_of_Francia">Independence and rule of Francia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Paraguay&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Independence and rule of Francia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Independence_of_Paraguay" title="Independence of Paraguay">Independence of Paraguay</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Jos%C3%A9_Gaspar_Rodr%C3%ADguez_de_Francia.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1681" data-file-width="1434" decoding="async" height="258" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Jos%C3%A9_Gaspar_Rodr%C3%ADguez_de_Francia.jpg/220px-Jos%C3%A9_Gaspar_Rodr%C3%ADguez_de_Francia.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Jos%C3%A9_Gaspar_Rodr%C3%ADguez_de_Francia.jpg/330px-Jos%C3%A9_Gaspar_Rodr%C3%ADguez_de_Francia.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Jos%C3%A9_Gaspar_Rodr%C3%ADguez_de_Francia.jpg/440px-Jos%C3%A9_Gaspar_Rodr%C3%ADguez_de_Francia.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Jos%C3%A9_Gaspar_Rodr%C3%ADguez_de_Francia.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Gaspar_Rodr%C3%ADguez_de_Francia" title="Jos&#233; Gaspar Rodr&#237;guez de Francia">Jos&#233; Gaspar Rodr&#237;guez de Francia</a>, Paraguay\'s first dictator.</div></div></div>\n<p>Paraguay overthrew the local Spanish administration on 14 May 1811. Paraguay\'s first dictator was <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Gaspar_Rodr%C3%ADguez_de_Francia" title="Jos&#233; Gaspar Rodr&#237;guez de Francia">Jos&#233; Gaspar Rodr&#237;guez de Francia</a> who ruled Paraguay from 1814 until his death in 1840, with very little outside contact or influence. He intended to create a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Utopian" title="Utopian">utopian</a> society based on the French theorist <a href="/wiki/Jean-Jacques_Rousseau" title="Jean-Jacques Rousseau">Jean-Jacques Rousseau</a>\'s <a href="/wiki/The_Social_Contract" title="The Social Contract"><i>Social Contract</i></a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[16]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Rodr&#237;guez de Francia established new laws that greatly reduced the powers of the Catholic church (Catholicism was then an established state religion) and the cabinet, forbade colonial citizens from marrying one another and allowed them to marry only blacks, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mulattoes" title="Mulattoes">mulattoes</a> or natives, in order to break the power of colonial-era elites and to create a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mixed-race" title="Mixed-race">mixed-race</a> or mestizo society.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[17]</a></sup> He cut off relations between Paraguay and the rest of South America. Because of Francia\'s restrictions of freedom, <a href="/wiki/Fulgencio_Yegros" title="Fulgencio Yegros">Fulgencio Yegros</a> and several other Independence-era leaders in 1820 planned a <i>coup d&#8217;&#233;tat</i> against Francia, who discovered the plot and had its leaders either executed or imprisoned for life.\n</p>\n<h3><span id="Rule_of_the_L.C3.B3pez_family"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Rule_of_the_L&#243;pez_family">Rule of the L&#243;pez family</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Paraguay&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Rule of the L&#243;pez family">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>After Francia\'s death in 1840, Paraguay was ruled by various military officers under a new <i><a href="/wiki/Military_junta" title="Military junta">junta</a></i>, until <a href="/wiki/Carlos_Antonio_L%C3%B3pez" title="Carlos Antonio L&#243;pez">Carlos Antonio L&#243;pez</a> (allegedly Rodr&#237;guez de Francia\'s nephew) came to power in 1841. L&#243;pez modernized Paraguay and opened it to foreign commerce. He signed a <a href="/wiki/Non-aggression_pact" title="Non-aggression pact">non-aggression pact</a> with Argentina and officially declared independence of Paraguay in 1842. After L&#243;pez\'s death in 1862, power was transferred to his eldest son, <a href="/wiki/Francisco_Solano_L%C3%B3pez" title="Francisco Solano L&#243;pez">Francisco Solano L&#243;pez</a>.\n</p><p>The regime of the L&#243;pez family was characterized by pervasive and rigid centralism in production and distribution. There was no distinction between the public and the private spheres, and the L&#243;pez family ruled the country as it would a large estate.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[18]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The government exerted control on all exports. The export of <a href="/wiki/Yerba_mate" title="Yerba mate">yerba mate</a> and valuable wood products maintained the balance of trade between Paraguay and the outside world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[19]</a></sup> The Paraguayan government was extremely protectionist, never accepted loans from abroad and levied high <a href="/wiki/Tariff" title="Tariff">tariffs</a> against imported foreign products. This <a href="/wiki/Protectionism" title="Protectionism">protectionism</a> made the society self-sufficient, and it also avoided the debt suffered by Argentina and Brazil. Slavery existed in Paraguay, although not in great numbers, until 1844, when it was legally abolished in the new Constitution.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECunninghame_Graham193339-40_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECunninghame_Graham193339-40-22">[20]</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Francisco_Solano_L%C3%B3pez" title="Francisco Solano L&#243;pez">Francisco Solano L&#243;pez</a>, the son of Carlos Antonio L&#243;pez, replaced his father as the President-Dictator in 1862, and generally continued the political policies of his father. Both wanted to give an international image of Paraguay as "democratic and republican", but in fact, the ruling family had almost total control of all public life in the country, including Church and colleges.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECunninghame_Graham193341-42_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECunninghame_Graham193341-42-23">[21]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Militarily, Carlos Antonio L&#243;pez modernized and expanded industry and the <a href="/wiki/Paraguayan_Army" title="Paraguayan Army">Paraguayan Army</a> and greatly strengthened the strategic defences of Paraguay by developing the <a href="/wiki/Fortress_of_Humait%C3%A1" title="Fortress of Humait&#225;">Fortress of Humait&#225;</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[22]</a></sup>  The government hired more than 200 foreign technicians, who installed <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Telegraph" title="Telegraph">telegraph</a> lines and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Railroad" title="Railroad">railroads</a> to aid the expanding steel, textile, paper and ink, naval construction, weapons and gunpowder industries.  The <a href="/wiki/Ybycu%C3%AD" title="Ybycu&#237;">Ybycu&#237;</a> foundry, completed in 1850, manufactured cannons, mortars and bullets of all calibers. River warships were built in the shipyards of Asunci&#243;n. Fortifications were built, especially along the <a href="/wiki/Apa_River" title="Apa River">Apa River</a> and in <a href="/wiki/Gran_Chaco" title="Gran Chaco">Gran Chaco</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hooker_25-0"><a href="#cite_note-Hooker-25">[23]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>22</span></sup>  The work was continued by his son Francisco Solano and in terms of socio-economic development, the country was dubbed as "the most advanced Republic in South America", notably by the British judge and politician <a href="/wiki/Robert_Phillimore" title="Robert Phillimore">Sir Robert Phillimore</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[24]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:1864_Mitchell_Map_of_Brazil,_Bolivia_and_Chili_-_Geographicus_-_SouthAmericaSouth-mitchell-1864.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3203" data-file-width="4000" decoding="async" height="176" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/1864_Mitchell_Map_of_Brazil%2C_Bolivia_and_Chili_-_Geographicus_-_SouthAmericaSouth-mitchell-1864.jpg/220px-1864_Mitchell_Map_of_Brazil%2C_Bolivia_and_Chili_-_Geographicus_-_SouthAmericaSouth-mitchell-1864.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/1864_Mitchell_Map_of_Brazil%2C_Bolivia_and_Chili_-_Geographicus_-_SouthAmericaSouth-mitchell-1864.jpg/330px-1864_Mitchell_Map_of_Brazil%2C_Bolivia_and_Chili_-_Geographicus_-_SouthAmericaSouth-mitchell-1864.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/1864_Mitchell_Map_of_Brazil%2C_Bolivia_and_Chili_-_Geographicus_-_SouthAmericaSouth-mitchell-1864.jpg/440px-1864_Mitchell_Map_of_Brazil%2C_Bolivia_and_Chili_-_Geographicus_-_SouthAmericaSouth-mitchell-1864.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:1864_Mitchell_Map_of_Brazil,_Bolivia_and_Chili_-_Geographicus_-_SouthAmericaSouth-mitchell-1864.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Political map of the region, 1864</div></div></div>\n<p>According to George Thompson, C.E., Lieutenant Colonel of Engineers in the Paraguayan Army prior to and during the war, L&#243;pez\'s government was comparatively a good one for Paraguay:\n</p>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r856303468">.mw-parser-output .templatequote{overflow:hidden;margin:1em 0;padding:0 40px}.mw-parser-output .templatequote .templatequotecite{line-height:1.5em;text-align:left;padding-left:1.6em;margin-top:0}</style><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>Probably in no other country in the world has life and property been so secure as all over Paraguay during his (Antonio Lopez\'s) reign. Crime was almost unknown, and when committed, immediately detected and punished. The mass of the people was, perhaps, the happiest in existence. They had hardly to do any work to gain a livelihood. Each family had its house or hut in its own ground. They planted, in a few days, enough tobacco, maize and mandioca for their own consumption [...]. Having at every hut a grove of oranges [...] and also a few cows, they were almost throughout the year under little necessity [...]. The higher classes, of course, lived more in the European way...</p><div class="templatequotecite">&#8212;&#8201;<cite>George Thompson, C.E.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEThompson186910_27-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEThompson186910-27">[25]</a></sup></cite></div>\n</blockquote>\n<h3><span id="Paraguayan_War_.281864.E2.80.931870.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Paraguayan_War_(1864&#8211;1870)">Paraguayan War (1864&#8211;1870)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Paraguay&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Paraguayan War (1864&#8211;1870)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Paraguayan_War" title="Paraguayan War">Paraguayan War</a> and <a href="/wiki/Paraguayan_War_casualties" title="Paraguayan War casualties">Paraguayan War casualties</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:FRANCISCO_SOLANO_LOPEZ_(From_a_Photograph_taken_in_1859).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1028" data-file-width="872" decoding="async" height="259" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/FRANCISCO_SOLANO_LOPEZ_%28From_a_Photograph_taken_in_1859%29.jpg/220px-FRANCISCO_SOLANO_LOPEZ_%28From_a_Photograph_taken_in_1859%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/FRANCISCO_SOLANO_LOPEZ_%28From_a_Photograph_taken_in_1859%29.jpg/330px-FRANCISCO_SOLANO_LOPEZ_%28From_a_Photograph_taken_in_1859%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/FRANCISCO_SOLANO_LOPEZ_%28From_a_Photograph_taken_in_1859%29.jpg/440px-FRANCISCO_SOLANO_LOPEZ_%28From_a_Photograph_taken_in_1859%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:FRANCISCO_SOLANO_LOPEZ_(From_a_Photograph_taken_in_1859).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Francisco_Solano_L%C3%B3pez" title="Francisco Solano L&#243;pez">Francisco Solano L&#243;pez</a></div></div></div>\n<p>On 12 October 1864, despite Paraguayan ultimatums, the <a href="/wiki/Empire_of_Brazil" title="Empire of Brazil">Brazilian Empire</a> (sided with the Argentine Government under Gen. <a href="/wiki/Bartolom%C3%A9_Mitre" title="Bartolom&#233; Mitre">Bartolom&#233; Mitre</a> and the rebellious <a href="/wiki/Colorado_Party_(Uruguay)" title="Colorado Party (Uruguay)">Uruguayan colorados</a> led by Gen. <a href="/wiki/Venancio_Flores" title="Venancio Flores">Venancio Flores</a>) invaded the Republic of Uruguay in order to overthrow the Government of that time (which was under the rule of the <a href="/wiki/National_Party_(Uruguay)" title="National Party (Uruguay)">Blanco Party</a>, an ally of L&#243;pez)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[26]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>, thus starting the <a href="/wiki/Paraguayan_War" title="Paraguayan War">Paraguayan War</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[27]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Paraguayans, led by the <a href="/wiki/Grand_marshal" title="Grand marshal">Marshal of the Republic</a> Francisco Solano L&#243;pez, retalliated by <a href="/wiki/Mato_Grosso_Campaign" title="Mato Grosso Campaign">attacking the Matto Grosso</a> on 15 December 1864 and later declared war against Argentina on 23 March 1865. The "Blanco Government" was toppled and replaced by a "Colorado Government" under Gen. Venancio Flores on 22 February 1865 and afterwards, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Argentine_Republic" title="Argentine Republic">Argentine Republic</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Empire_of_Brazil" title="Empire of Brazil">Empire of Brazil</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Republic_of_Uruguay" title="Republic of Uruguay">Republic of Uruguay</a> signed the infamous <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_the_Triple_Alliance" title="Treaty of the Triple Alliance">Secret Treaty of the Triple Alliance</a> against the Paraguayan Government, on 1 May 1865.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[28]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Paraguayans held a ferocious resistance but were ultimately defeated in 1870 after the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Cerro_Cor%C3%A1" title="Battle of Cerro Cor&#225;">Battle of Cerro Cor&#225;</a>, where Marshal Solano L&#243;pez was killed in action, refusing to surrender.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[29]</a></sup> The real causes of this war, which remains the bloodiest international conflict in the history of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Americas" title="The Americas">The Americas</a>, are still highly debated.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[30]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Paraguay lost around 25 - 33% of its territory to Argentina and Brazil, was forced to pay an enormous war debt and to sell large amounts of national properties in order to restore its internal budget. But the worst consequence of the war was the catastrophic loss of population. At least 50% of the Paraguayans died during the conflict and took long decades for the country to recover. About the disaster suffered by the Paraguayans at the outcome of the war, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/William_D._Rubinstein" title="William D. Rubinstein">William D. Rubinstein</a> wrote:\n</p><p><i>"The normal estimate is that of a Paraguayan population of somewhere between 450,000 and 900,000, only 220,000 survived the war, of whom only 28,000 were adult males."</i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[31]</a></sup>\n</p><p>During the pillaging of Asunci&#243;n in 1869, the <a href="/wiki/Imperial_Brazilian_Army" title="Imperial Brazilian Army">Imperial Brazilian Army</a> packed up and transported the Paraguayan National Archives to <a href="/wiki/Rio_de_Janeiro" title="Rio de Janeiro">Rio de Janeiro</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[32]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[33]</a></sup> Brazil\'s records from the war have remained classified.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[34]</a></sup> This has made Paraguayan history in the Colonial and early National periods difficult to research and study.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:TuyutiDetail.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="945" data-file-width="1446" decoding="async" height="144" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/TuyutiDetail.jpg/220px-TuyutiDetail.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/TuyutiDetail.jpg/330px-TuyutiDetail.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/TuyutiDetail.jpg/440px-TuyutiDetail.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:TuyutiDetail.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Tuyut%C3%AD" title="Battle of Tuyut&#237;">Battle of Tuyut&#237;</a>, May 1866</div></div></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="20th_century">20th century</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Paraguay&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: 20th century">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Chacokrieg.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="313" data-file-width="300" decoding="async" height="230" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Chacokrieg.jpg/220px-Chacokrieg.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/f/f4/Chacokrieg.jpg 1.5x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Chacokrieg.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Gran_Chaco" title="Gran Chaco">Gran Chaco</a> was the site of the <a href="/wiki/Chaco_War" title="Chaco War">Chaco War</a> (1932&#8211;35), in which Bolivia lost most of the disputed territory to Paraguay.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Recrutas_paraguaios..jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="500" data-file-width="662" decoding="async" height="166" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Recrutas_paraguaios..jpg/220px-Recrutas_paraguaios..jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Recrutas_paraguaios..jpg/330px-Recrutas_paraguaios..jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Recrutas_paraguaios..jpg/440px-Recrutas_paraguaios..jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Recrutas_paraguaios..jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Paraguayan recruits during the Chaco war</div></div></div>\n<p>In 1904 the Liberal revolution against the rule of Colorados broke out. The Liberal rule started a period of great political instability. Between 1904 and 1954 Paraguay had thirty-one <a href="/wiki/President_of_Paraguay" title="President of Paraguay">presidents</a>, most of whom were removed from office by force.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[35]</a></sup> Conflicts between the factions of the ruling Liberal party led to the <a href="/wiki/Paraguayan_Civil_War_(1922)" title="Paraguayan Civil War (1922)">Paraguayan Civil War of 1922</a>.\n</p><p>The unresolved border conflict with Bolivia over the Chaco region finally erupted in the early 1930s in the <a href="/wiki/Chaco_War" title="Chaco War">Chaco War</a>. After great losses Paraguay defeated Bolivia and established its sovereignty over most of the disputed Chaco region. After the war, military officers used popular dissatisfaction with the Liberal politicians to seize the power for themselves. On 17 February 1936, the <a href="/wiki/February_Revolution_(Paraguay)" title="February Revolution (Paraguay)">February Revolution</a> brought colonel <a href="/wiki/Rafael_Franco" title="Rafael Franco">Rafael Franco</a> to power. Between 1940 and 1948, the country was ruled by general <a href="/wiki/Higinio_Mor%C3%ADnigo" title="Higinio Mor&#237;nigo">Higinio Mor&#237;nigo</a>. Dissatisfaction with his rule resulted in the <a href="/wiki/Paraguayan_Civil_War_(1947)" title="Paraguayan Civil War (1947)">Paraguayan civil war of 1947</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[36]</a></sup> In its aftermath <a href="/wiki/Alfredo_Stroessner" title="Alfredo Stroessner">Alfredo Stroessner</a> began involvement in a string of plots, which resulted in his military <a href="/wiki/Coup_d%27%C3%A9tat" title="Coup d\'&#233;tat">coup d\'&#233;tat</a> of 4 May 1954.\n</p>\n<h3><span id="Stroessner_era.2C_1954.E2.80.931989"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Stroessner_era,_1954&#8211;1989">Stroessner era, 1954&#8211;1989</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Paraguay&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Stroessner era, 1954&#8211;1989">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/El_Stronato" title="El Stronato">El Stronato</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Alfredo_Stroessner_Paraguay_stamp.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="599" data-file-width="478" decoding="async" height="251" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Alfredo_Stroessner_Paraguay_stamp.jpg/200px-Alfredo_Stroessner_Paraguay_stamp.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Alfredo_Stroessner_Paraguay_stamp.jpg/300px-Alfredo_Stroessner_Paraguay_stamp.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Alfredo_Stroessner_Paraguay_stamp.jpg/400px-Alfredo_Stroessner_Paraguay_stamp.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Alfredo_Stroessner_Paraguay_stamp.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Alfredo_Stroessner" title="Alfredo Stroessner">Alfredo Stroessner</a>, Paraguayan dictator from 1954 to 1989</div></div></div>\n<p>A series of unstable governments ensued until the establishment in 1954 of the regime of dictator <a href="/wiki/Alfredo_Stroessner" title="Alfredo Stroessner">Alfredo Stroessner</a>, who remained in office for more than three decades until 1989. Paraguay was modernized to some extent under Stroessner\'s regime, although his rule was marked by extensive human rights abuses.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[37]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Stroessner and the <i>Colorado</i> party ruled the country from 1954 to 1989. The dictator oversaw an era of economic expansion, but also had a poor human rights and environmental record (see "Political History"). Paraguay actively participated in <a href="/wiki/Operation_Condor" title="Operation Condor">Operation Condor</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[38]</a></sup> Torture and death for political opponents was routine. After his overthrow, the <i>Colorado</i> continued to dominate national politics until 2008.\n</p><p>The splits in the <i>Colorado</i> Party in the 1980s, and the prevailing conditions: Stroessner\'s advanced age, the character of the regime, the economic downturn, and <a href="/wiki/International_isolation" title="International isolation">international isolation</a>, were catalysts for anti-regime demonstrations and statements by the opposition prior to the 1988 general elections.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>\n</p><p><i><a href="/wiki/Authentic_Radical_Liberal_Party" title="Authentic Radical Liberal Party">PLRA</a></i> leader <a href="/wiki/Domingo_La%C3%ADno" title="Domingo La&#237;no">Domingo La&#237;no</a> served as the focal point of the opposition in the second half of the 1980s. The government\'s effort to isolate Laino by exiling him in 1982 had backfired. On his sixth attempt to re-enter the country in 1986, Laino returned with three television crews from the U.S., a former United States ambassador to Paraguay, and a group of Uruguayan and Argentine congressmen. Despite the international contingent, the police violently barred Laino\'s return.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>\n</p><p>The Stroessner regime relented in April 1987, and permitted Laino to return to Asunci&#243;n. Laino took the lead in organizing demonstrations and reducing infighting among the opposition party. The opposition was unable to reach agreement on a common strategy regarding the elections, with some parties advocating abstention, and others calling for blank voting. The parties held numerous \'lightning demonstrations\' (<i>m&#237;tines rel&#225;mpagos</i>), especially in rural areas. Such demonstrations were gathered and quickly disbanded before the arrival of the police.\n</p><p>In response to the upsurge in opposition activities, Stroessner condemned the Accord for advocating "sabotage of the general elections and disrespect of the law".  He used national police and civilian <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vigilantes" title="Vigilantes">vigilantes</a> of the <i>Colorado</i> Party to break up demonstrations. A number of opposition leaders were imprisoned or otherwise harassed. <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Hermes_Rafael_Saguier&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Hermes Rafael Saguier (page does not exist)">Hermes Rafael Saguier</a>, another key leader of the <i>PLRA</i>, was imprisoned for four months in 1987 on charges of sedition. In early February 1988, police arrested 200 people attending a National Coordinating Committee meeting in <a href="/wiki/Coronel_Oviedo" title="Coronel Oviedo">Coronel Oviedo</a>. Laino and several other opposition figures were arrested before dawn on the day of the election, 14 February, and held for twelve hours. The government declared Stroessner\'s re-election with 89% of the vote.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[39]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The opposition attributed the results in part to the virtual Colorado monopoly on the mass media. They noted that 53% of those polled indicated that there was an "uneasiness" in Paraguayan society. 74% believed that the political situation needed changes, including 45% who wanted a substantial or total change. Finally, 31% stated that they planned to abstain from voting in the February elections.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2008)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id="Stroessner.27s_overthrow.2C_post-1989"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Stroessner\'s_overthrow,_post-1989">Stroessner\'s overthrow, post-1989</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Paraguay&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Stroessner\'s overthrow, post-1989">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>On 3 February 1989, Stroessner was overthrown in a military coup headed by General <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Andr%C3%A9s_Rodr%C3%ADguez_(President)" title="Andr&#233;s Rodr&#237;guez (President)">Andr&#233;s Rodr&#237;guez</a>. As president, Rodr&#237;guez instituted political, legal, and economic reforms and initiated a <i>rapprochement</i> with the international community. Reflecting the deep hunger of the rural poor for land, hundreds immediately occupied thousands of acres of unused territories belonging to Stroessner and his associates; by mid-1990, 19,000 families occupied 340,000 acres (138,000&#160;ha). At the time, 2.06 million people lived in rural areas, more than half of the 4.1 million total population, and most were landless.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nagel_42-0"><a href="#cite_note-nagel-42">[40]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The June 1992 constitution established a democratic system of government and dramatically improved protection of fundamental human rights. In May 1993, Colorado Party candidate <a href="/wiki/Juan_Carlos_Wasmosy" title="Juan Carlos Wasmosy">Juan Carlos Wasmosy</a> was elected as Paraguay\'s first civilian president in almost 40 years, in what international observers deemed fair and free elections.\n</p><p>With support from the United States, the Organization of American States, and other countries in the region, the Paraguayan people rejected an April 1996 attempt by then Army Chief General <a href="/wiki/Lino_Oviedo" title="Lino Oviedo">Lino Oviedo</a> to oust President Wasmosy.\n</p><p>Oviedo was nominated as the Colorado candidate for president in the 1998 election, however, when the Supreme Court upheld in April his conviction on charges related to the 1996 coup attempt, he was not allowed to run and was detained in jail. His former running mate, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ra%C3%BAl_Cubas" title="Ra&#250;l Cubas">Ra&#250;l Cubas</a>, became the Colorado Party\'s candidate, and was elected in May in elections deemed by international observers to be free and fair. One of Cubas\' first acts after taking office in August was to commute Oviedo\'s sentence and release him. In December 1998, Paraguay\'s Supreme Court declared these actions unconstitutional. In this tense atmosphere, the murder of Vice President and long-time Oviedo rival <a href="/wiki/Luis_Mar%C3%ADa_Arga%C3%B1a" title="Luis Mar&#237;a Arga&#241;a">Luis Mar&#237;a Arga&#241;a</a> on 23 March 1999, led the Chamber of Deputies to impeach Cubas the next day.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> On 26 March, eight student anti-government demonstrators were murdered, widely believed to have been carried out by Oviedo supporters. This increased opposition to Cubas, who resigned on 28 March. Senate President <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Luis_Gonz%C3%A1lez_Macchi" title="Luis Gonz&#225;lez Macchi">Luis Gonz&#225;lez Macchi</a>, a Cubas opponent, was peacefully sworn in as president the same day.\n</p><p>In 2003, Nicanor Duarte Frutos was elected as president.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Election_of_Fernando_Lugo">Election of Fernando Lugo</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Paraguay&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Election of Fernando Lugo">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>For the 2008 general elections, the Colorado Party was favored in polls. Their candidate was Minister of Education <a href="/wiki/Blanca_Ovelar" title="Blanca Ovelar">Blanca Ovelar</a>, the first woman to be nominated as a candidate for a major party in Paraguayan history. After sixty years of Colorado rule, voters chose <a href="/wiki/Fernando_Lugo" title="Fernando Lugo">Fernando Lugo</a>, a former Roman Catholic Bishop and not a professional politician in civil government, and a member of the Authentic Radical Liberal Party, Paraguay\'s largest opposition party. Lugo was an adherent of <a href="/wiki/Liberation_theology" title="Liberation theology">liberation theology</a>. Lugo achieved a historic victory in Paraguay\'s presidential election, defeating the ruling party candidate, and ending 61 years of conservative rule. Lugo won with nearly 41% of the vote, compared to almost 31% for Blanca Ovelar of the Colorado party.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[41]</a></sup> Outgoing President Nicanor Duarte Frutos hailed the moment as the first time in the history of the nation that a government had transferred power to opposition forces in a constitutional and peaceful fashion.\n</p><p>Lugo was sworn in on 15 August 2008. The Lugo administration set its two major priorities as the reduction of corruption and economic inequality.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-state.gov_44-0"><a href="#cite_note-state.gov-44">[42]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Saludo_de_Pi%C3%B1era_a_Cartes.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="380" data-file-width="720" decoding="async" height="116" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Saludo_de_Pi%C3%B1era_a_Cartes.jpg/220px-Saludo_de_Pi%C3%B1era_a_Cartes.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Saludo_de_Pi%C3%B1era_a_Cartes.jpg/330px-Saludo_de_Pi%C3%B1era_a_Cartes.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Saludo_de_Pi%C3%B1era_a_Cartes.jpg/440px-Saludo_de_Pi%C3%B1era_a_Cartes.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Saludo_de_Pi%C3%B1era_a_Cartes.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Inauguration of former President <a href="/wiki/Horacio_Cartes" title="Horacio Cartes">Horacio Cartes</a>, 15 August 2013</div></div></div>\n<p>Political instability following Lugo\'s election and disputes within his cabinet encouraged some renewal of popular support for the Colorado Party. Reports suggested that the businessman Horacio Cartes became the new political figure amid disputes. Despite the US <a href="/wiki/Drug_Enforcement_Administration" title="Drug Enforcement Administration">Drug Enforcement Administration</a>\'s strong accusations against Cartes related to drug trafficking, he continued to amass followers in the political arena.\n</p><p>On 14 January 2011, the Colorado Party convention nominated Horacio Cartes as the presidential candidate for the party. However, the party\'s constitution didn\'t allow it.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (April 2012)">clarification needed</span></a></i>]</sup>\nOn 21 June 2012, <a href="/wiki/Impeachment_of_Fernando_Lugo" title="Impeachment of Fernando Lugo">impeachment proceedings against President Lugo</a> began in the country\'s lower house, which was controlled by his opponents. Lugo was given less than twenty-four hours to prepare for the proceedings and only two hours in which to mount a defense.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Guardian_45-0"><a href="#cite_note-Guardian-45">[43]</a></sup> Impeachment was quickly approved and the resulting trial in Paraguay\'s Senate, also controlled by the opposition, ended with the removal of Lugo from office and Vice President Federico Franco assuming the duties of president.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CNN22_46-0"><a href="#cite_note-CNN22-46">[44]</a></sup> Lugo\'s rivals blamed him for the deaths of 17 people &#8211; eight police officers and nine farmers &#8211; in armed clashes after police were ambushed by armed peasants when enforcing an eviction order against rural trespassers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[45]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Lugo\'s supporters gathered outside Congress to protest the decision as a "politically motivated coup d\'&#233;tat".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CNN22_46-1"><a href="#cite_note-CNN22-46">[44]</a></sup> Lugo\'s removal from office on 22 June 2012 is considered by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UNASUR" title="UNASUR">UNASUR</a> and other neighboring countries, especially those currently governed by leftist leaders, as a coup d\'&#233;tat.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[46]</a></sup> However, the Organization of American States, which sent a mission to Paraguay to gather information, concluded that the impeachment process was not a coup d\'&#233;tat, as it had been carried out in accordance with the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Paraguay" title="Constitution of Paraguay">Constitution of Paraguay</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[47]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Present_day">Present day</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Paraguay&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Present day">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>From August 2013 to 15 August 2018, the  <a href="/wiki/President_of_Paraguay" title="President of Paraguay">President of Paraguay</a> was <a href="/wiki/Horacio_Cartes" title="Horacio Cartes">Horacio Cartes</a>.\n</p><p>Since 15 August 2018  the current <a href="/wiki/President_of_Paraguay" title="President of Paraguay">President of Paraguay</a> is  <a href="/wiki/Mario_Abdo_Ben%C3%ADtez" title="Mario Abdo Ben&#237;tez">Mario Abdo Ben&#237;tez</a>.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography_and_climate">Geography and climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Paraguay&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Geography and climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Paraguay&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Paraguay" title="Geography of Paraguay">Geography of Paraguay</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Paraguay_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1900" data-file-width="1900" decoding="async" height="220" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Paraguay_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg/220px-Paraguay_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Paraguay_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg/330px-Paraguay_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Paraguay_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg/440px-Paraguay_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Paraguay_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Paraguay map of K&#246;ppen climate classification</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Chaco_Boreal_Paraguay.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1200" data-file-width="1600" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Chaco_Boreal_Paraguay.jpg/220px-Chaco_Boreal_Paraguay.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Chaco_Boreal_Paraguay.jpg/330px-Chaco_Boreal_Paraguay.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Chaco_Boreal_Paraguay.jpg/440px-Chaco_Boreal_Paraguay.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Chaco_Boreal_Paraguay.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Landscape in the <a href="/wiki/Gran_Chaco" title="Gran Chaco">Gran Chaco</a>, Paraguay</div></div></div>\n<p>Paraguay is divided by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/R%C3%ADo_Paraguay" title="R&#237;o Paraguay">R&#237;o Paraguay</a> into two well differentiated geographic regions. The eastern region (Regi&#243;n Oriental); and the western region, officially called Western Paraguay (Regi&#243;n Occidental) and also known as the Chaco, which is part of the <a href="/wiki/Gran_Chaco" title="Gran Chaco">Gran Chaco</a>. The country lies between latitudes <a href="/wiki/19th_parallel_south" title="19th parallel south">19&#176;</a> and <a href="/wiki/28th_parallel_south" title="28th parallel south">28&#176;S</a>, and longitudes <a href="/wiki/54th_meridian_west" title="54th meridian west">54&#176;</a> and <a href="/wiki/63rd_meridian_west" title="63rd meridian west">63&#176;W</a>.\nThe terrain consists mostly of grassy plains and wooded hills in the eastern region. To the west are mostly low, marshy plains.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Paraguay&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Climate_of_Paraguay" title="Climate of Paraguay">Climate of Paraguay</a></div>\n<p>The overall climate is <a href="/wiki/Tropical_climate" title="Tropical climate">tropical</a> to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Subtropical_climate" title="Subtropical climate">subtropical</a>. Like most lands in the region, Paraguay has only wet and dry periods. Winds play a major role in influencing Paraguay\'s weather: between October and March, warm winds blow from the Amazon Basin in the North, while the period between May and August brings cold winds from the Andes.\n</p><p>The absence of mountain ranges to provide a natural barrier allows winds to develop speeds as high as 161&#160;km/h (100&#160;mph). This also leads to significant changes in temperature within a short span of time; between April and September, temperatures will sometimes drop below freezing. January is the hottest summer month, with an average daily temperature of 28.9 degrees Celsius (84 degrees F).\n</p><p>Rainfall varies dramatically across the country, with substantial rainfall in the eastern portions, and semi-arid conditions in the far west. The far eastern forest belt receives an average of 170 centimeters (67 inches) of rain annually, while the western Chaco region typically averages no more than 50&#160;cm (20&#160;in) a year. The rains in the west tend to be irregular and evaporate quickly, contributing to the aridity of the area.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Government_and_politics">Government and politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Paraguay&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Government and politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Paraguay" title="Politics of Paraguay">Politics of Paraguay</a>, <a href="/wiki/Human_rights_in_Paraguay" title="Human rights in Paraguay">Human rights in Paraguay</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Paraguay" title="Foreign relations of Paraguay">Foreign relations of Paraguay</a></div>\n<p>Paraguay is a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Representative_democratic" title="Representative democratic">representative democratic</a> republic, with a multi-party system and <a href="/wiki/Separation_of_powers" title="Separation of powers">separation of powers</a> in three branches. Executive power is exercised solely by the <a href="/wiki/President_of_Paraguay" title="President of Paraguay">President</a>, who is <a href="/wiki/Head_of_state" title="Head of state">head of state</a> and <a href="/wiki/Head_of_government" title="Head of government">head of government</a>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Legislative_power" title="Legislative power">Legislative power</a> is vested in the two chambers of the <a href="/wiki/Congress_of_Paraguay" title="Congress of Paraguay">National Congress</a>. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Judicial_Branch" title="Judicial Branch">judiciary</a> is vested on <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tribunals" title="Tribunals">tribunals</a> and Courts of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Civil_Law_(legal_system)" title="Civil Law (legal system)">Civil Law</a> and a nine-member Supreme Court of Justice, all of them independent of the executive and the legislature.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Military">Military</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Paraguay&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Military">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Military_of_Paraguay" title="Military of Paraguay">Military of Paraguay</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Paraguayan_marines_at_Ancon_Marine_Base_2010-07-19.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2848" data-file-width="4288" decoding="async" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Paraguayan_marines_at_Ancon_Marine_Base_2010-07-19.JPG/220px-Paraguayan_marines_at_Ancon_Marine_Base_2010-07-19.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Paraguayan_marines_at_Ancon_Marine_Base_2010-07-19.JPG/330px-Paraguayan_marines_at_Ancon_Marine_Base_2010-07-19.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Paraguayan_marines_at_Ancon_Marine_Base_2010-07-19.JPG/440px-Paraguayan_marines_at_Ancon_Marine_Base_2010-07-19.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Paraguayan_marines_at_Ancon_Marine_Base_2010-07-19.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Paraguayan marines at Ancon Marine Base</div></div></div>\n<p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Military_of_Paraguay" title="Military of Paraguay">military of Paraguay</a> consist of the Paraguayan <a href="/wiki/Army" title="Army">army</a>, <a href="/wiki/Navy" title="Navy">navy</a> (including <a href="/wiki/Naval_aviation" title="Naval aviation">naval aviation</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Marine_corps" title="Marine corps">marine corps</a>) and <a href="/wiki/Air_force" title="Air force">air force</a>.\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Paraguay" title="Constitution of Paraguay">constitution of Paraguay</a> (article 238) establishes the <a href="/wiki/President_of_Paraguay" title="President of Paraguay">president of Paraguay</a> as the <a href="/wiki/Commander-in-chief" title="Commander-in-chief">commander-in-chief</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[48]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Paraguay has <a href="/wiki/Conscription" title="Conscription">compulsory military service</a>, and all 18-year-old males and 17-year-olds in the year of their 18th birthday are liable for one year of <a href="/wiki/Active_duty" title="Active duty">active duty</a>. Although the 1992 constitution allows for conscientious objection, no enabling legislation has yet been approved.\n</p><p>In July 2005, military aid in the form of U.S. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Special_Forces" title="Special Forces">Special Forces</a> began arriving at Paraguay\'s <a href="/wiki/Mariscal_Estigarribia" title="Mariscal Estigarribia">Mariscal Estigarribia</a> air base, a sprawling complex built in 1982.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[49]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Clarin_52-0"><a href="#cite_note-Clarin-52">[50]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_subdivisions">Administrative subdivisions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Paraguay&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Administrative subdivisions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Departments_of_Paraguay" title="Departments of Paraguay">Departments of Paraguay</a> and <a href="/wiki/Districts_of_Paraguay" title="Districts of Paraguay">Districts of Paraguay</a></div>\n<p>Paraguay consists of seventeen departments and one capital district (<i>distrito capital</i>).\n</p><p>It is also divided into 2 regions: The "Occidental Region" or Chaco (Boquer&#243;n, Alto Paraguay and Presidente Hayes), and the "Oriental Region" (the other departments and the capital district).\n</p><p>These are the departments, with their capitals, population, area and the number of districts:\n</p>\n<div class="noresize" role="img" (<i>distritos</i>).\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Paraguay&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Paraguay" title="Economy of Paraguay">Economy of Paraguay</a></div>\n<p>Between 1970 and 2013, the country had the highest economic growth of South America,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> with an average rate of 7.2% per year.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> In 2010 and 2013, Paraguay experienced the greatest economic expansion of South America, with a GDP growth rate of 14.5% and 13.6% respectively.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[51]</a></sup>\n</p><p>99.9% of <a href="/wiki/Electricity_sector_in_Paraguay" title="Electricity sector in Paraguay">Paraguay\'s electricity</a> is produced using <a href="/wiki/Hydroelectricity" title="Hydroelectricity">hydroelectricity</a>, making it one of the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_electricity_production_from_renewable_sources" title="List of countries by electricity production from renewable sources">cleanest in the world</a>. Paraguay has an installed electrical production capacity of 8,110 MW, producing 63 billion kWh/year in 2016; with domestic consumption of just 15 billion kWh, the excess production is sold to Brazil, Argentina, and Uruguay, making Paraguay the world\'s largest exporter of electric power.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[52]</a></sup> This production is from two large <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hydroelectric_power" title="Hydroelectric power">hydroelectric power</a> projects along its borders, including the <a href="/wiki/Itaipu_Dam" title="Itaipu Dam">Itaipu Dam</a>, the world\'s second largest generating station. \n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Paraguay_Export_Treemap.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="667" data-file-width="854" decoding="async" height="172" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Paraguay_Export_Treemap.png/220px-Paraguay_Export_Treemap.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Paraguay_Export_Treemap.png/330px-Paraguay_Export_Treemap.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Paraguay_Export_Treemap.png/440px-Paraguay_Export_Treemap.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Paraguay_Export_Treemap.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Graphical depiction of Paraguay\'s product exports in 28 color-coded categories, 2012</div></div></div>\n<p>Paraguay is the sixth-largest <a href="/wiki/Soybean" title="Soybean">soybean</a> producer in the world,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[53]</a></sup> second-largest producer of <a href="/wiki/Stevia" title="Stevia">stevia</a>, second-largest producer of <a href="/wiki/Tung_oil" title="Tung oil">tung oil</a>, sixth-largest exporter of corn, tenth-largest exporter of wheat and 8th largest exporter of beef.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>\n</p><p>The market economy is distinguished by a large informal sector, featuring re-export of imported consumer goods to neighboring countries, as well as the activities of thousands of microenterprises and urban street vendors. Nonetheless, over the last 10 years the Paraguayan economy diversified dramatically, with the energy, auto parts and clothing industries leading the way.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[54]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The country also boasts the third most important free commercial zone in the world: <a href="/wiki/Ciudad_del_Este" title="Ciudad del Este">Ciudad del Este</a>, trailing behind <a href="/wiki/Miami" title="Miami">Miami</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong" title="Hong Kong">Hong Kong</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[55]</a></sup> A large percentage of the population, especially in rural areas, derives its living from agricultural activity, often on a subsistence basis. Because of the importance of the informal sector, accurate economic measures are difficult to obtain. The economy grew rapidly between 2003 and 2013 as growing world demand for commodities combined with high prices and favorable weather to support Paraguay\'s commodity-based export expansion.\n</p><p>In 2012, Paraguay\'s government introduced the MERCOSUR(FOCEM) system in order to stimulate the economy and job growth through a partnership with both Brazil and Argentina.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[56]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Industry_and_manufacturing">Industry and manufacturing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Paraguay&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Industry and manufacturing">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:BBVA_Paraguay.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2722" data-file-width="1815" decoding="async" height="330" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/BBVA_Paraguay.jpg/220px-BBVA_Paraguay.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/BBVA_Paraguay.jpg/330px-BBVA_Paraguay.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/BBVA_Paraguay.jpg/440px-BBVA_Paraguay.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:BBVA_Paraguay.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Banco_Bilbao_Vizcaya_Argentaria" title="Banco Bilbao Vizcaya Argentaria">BBVA</a> Paraguay</div></div></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Mineral_industry_of_Paraguay" title="Mineral industry of Paraguay">mineral industry of Paraguay</a> produces about 25% of the country\'s gross domestic product (GDP) and employs about 31% of the labor force. Production of <a href="/wiki/Cement" title="Cement">cement</a>, <a href="/wiki/Iron_ore" title="Iron ore">iron ore</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Steel" title="Steel">steel</a> occurs commonly throughout Paraguay\'s industrial sector. The growth of the industry was further fueled by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Maquila" title="Maquila">maquila</a> industry, with large industrial complexes located in the eastern part of the country. Paraguay put in place many incentives aimed to attract industries to the country. One of them is the so-called "Maquila law" by which companies can relocate to Paraguay, enjoying minimal tax rates.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[57]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In the <a href="/wiki/Pharmaceutical_industry" title="Pharmaceutical industry">pharmaceutical industry</a>, Paraguayan companies now<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The time period mentioned near this tag is ambiguous. (February 2016)">when?</span></a></i>]</sup> meet 70% of domestic consumption and have begun to <a href="/wiki/Export" title="Export">export</a> drugs. Paraguay is quickly<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="This term requires quantification. (February 2016)">quantify</span></a></i>]</sup> supplanting foreign suppliers in meeting the country\'s drug needs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[58]</a></sup> Strong growth also is evident in the production of edible oils, garments, organic sugar, meat processing, and steel.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>\n</p><p>In 2003 manufacturing made up 13.6% of the GDP, and the sector employed about 11% of the working population in 2000. Paraguay\'s primary manufacturing focus is on food and beverages. Wood products, paper products, hides and furs, and non-metallic mineral products also contribute to manufacturing totals. Steady growth in the manufacturing GDP during the 1990s (1.2% annually) laid the foundation for 2002 and 2003, when the annual growth rate rose to 2.5%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[59]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Social_issues">Social issues</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Paraguay&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Social issues">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="box-Update plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Update" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><img alt="Ambox current red.svg" data-file-height="290" data-file-width="360" decoding="async" height="34" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Ambox_current_red.svg/42px-Ambox_current_red.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Ambox_current_red.svg/63px-Ambox_current_red.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Ambox_current_red.svg/84px-Ambox_current_red.svg.png 2x" width="42"/></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section needs to be <b>updated</b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please update this article to reflect recent events or newly available information.</span> <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">April 2014</span>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>Various poverty estimates suggest that 30&#8211;50% of the population is poor.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[60]</a></sup> In rural areas, 41.20% of the people lack a monthly income to cover basic necessities, whereas in urban centers this figure is 27.6%. The top 10% of the population holds 43.8% of the national income, while the lowest 10% has 0.5%. The economic recession has worsened income inequality, notably in the rural areas, where the <a href="/wiki/Gini_coefficient" title="Gini coefficient">Gini coefficient</a> has risen from 0.56 in 1995 to 0.66 in 1999.\n</p><p>More recent data (2009)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-abc.com.py_63-0"><a href="#cite_note-abc.com.py-63">[61]</a></sup> show that 35% of the Paraguayan population is poor, 19% of which live in extreme poverty. Moreover, 71% of the latter live in rural areas of the country.\n</p><p>Similarly, land concentration in the Paraguayan countryside is one of the highest in the globe: 10% of the population controls 66% of the land, while 30% of the rural people are landless.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[62]</a></sup> In the immediate aftermath of the 1989 overthrow of Stroessner, some 19,000 rural families occupied hundreds of thousands of acres of unused lands formerly held by the dictator and his associates by mid-1990, but many rural poor remained landless. This inequality has caused a great deal of tensions between the landless and land owners.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nagel_42-1"><a href="#cite_note-nagel-42">[40]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Social_issues_of_the_indigenous">Social issues of the indigenous</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Paraguay&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Social issues of the indigenous">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>Literacy rates are extremely low among Paraguay\'s indigenous population, who have an illiteracy rate of 51% compared to the 7.1% rate of the general population.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-paho_65-0"><a href="#cite_note-paho-65">[63]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Only 2.5% of Paraguay\'s indigenous population has access to clean drinking water and only 9.5% have electricity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-paho_65-1"><a href="#cite_note-paho-65">[63]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Paraguay&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Paraguay" title="Demographics of Paraguay">Demographics of Paraguay</a> and <a href="/wiki/Immigration_to_Paraguay" title="Immigration to Paraguay">Immigration to Paraguay</a></div>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_most_common_surnames_in_South_America#Paraguay" title="List of most common surnames in South America">List of most common surnames in Paraguay</a></div>\n<table class="box-Multiple_issues plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-multiple_issues compact-ambox" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div href="/wiki/File:Paraguay_population_density.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="823" data-file-width="1030" decoding="async" height="176"
