//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Paraguay_population_density.png/440px-Paraguay_population_density.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Paraguay_population_density.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Paraguay population density (people per km<sup>2</sup>)</div></div></div>\n<table class="wikitable" style="float: right; margin-left: 10px">\n<tbody><tr>\n<th colspan="4" style="text-align:center; background:#cfb;">Population<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UN_WPP_66-0"><a href="#cite_note-UN_WPP-66">[64]</a></sup>\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<th style="background:#cfb;">Year\n</th>\n<th style="background:#cfb;">Million\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="text-align:left;">1950</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">1.5\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="text-align:left;">2000</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">5.3\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="text-align:left;">2016</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">6.7\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bev%C3%B6lkerungspyramide_Paraguay_2016.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="425" data-file-width="610" decoding="async" height="153" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Bev%C3%B6lkerungspyramide_Paraguay_2016.png/220px-Bev%C3%B6lkerungspyramide_Paraguay_2016.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Bev%C3%B6lkerungspyramide_Paraguay_2016.png/330px-Bev%C3%B6lkerungspyramide_Paraguay_2016.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Bev%C3%B6lkerungspyramide_Paraguay_2016.png/440px-Bev%C3%B6lkerungspyramide_Paraguay_2016.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bev%C3%B6lkerungspyramide_Paraguay_2016.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Population pyramid 2016</div></div></div>\n<p>Paraguay\'s population is distributed unevenly through the country, with the vast majority of people living in the eastern region near the capital and largest city, <a href="/wiki/Asunci%C3%B3n" title="Asunci&#243;n">Asunci&#243;n</a>, which accounts for 10% of the country\'s population. The <a href="/wiki/Gran_Chaco" title="Gran Chaco">Gran Chaco</a> region, which includes the <a href="/wiki/Alto_Paraguay_Department" title="Alto Paraguay Department">Alto Paraguay</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Boquer%C3%B3n_Department" title="Boquer&#243;n Department">Boquer&#243;n</a> and <a href="/wiki/Presidente_Hayes_Department" title="Presidente Hayes Department">Presidente Hayes Department</a>, and accounts for about 60% of the territory, is home to less than 2% of the population. About 56% of Paraguayans live in urban areas, making Paraguay one of the least urbanized nations in South America.\n</p><p>For most of its history, Paraguay has been a recipient of immigrants, owing to its low population density, especially after the demographic collapse that resulted from the Paraguayan War. Small groups of ethnic Italians, Germans, Russians, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Japanese_Paraguayan" title="Japanese Paraguayan">Japanese</a>, <a href="/wiki/Koreans_in_Paraguay" title="Koreans in Paraguay">Koreans</a>, Chinese, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lebanese_migration_to_Paraguay" title="Lebanese migration to Paraguay">Arabs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ukrainians_in_Paraguay" title="Ukrainians in Paraguay">Ukrainians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Poles" title="Poles">Poles</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jews" title="Jews">Jews</a>, Brazilians, and Argentines have also settled in Paraguay. Around 40% of the total Paraguayan population has some <a href="/wiki/Italians_in_Paraguay" title="Italians in Paraguay">Italian descent</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[65]</a></sup> Paraguay has also been a haven for communities persecuted for the religious faith, like the <a href="/wiki/Bruderhof_Communities" title="Bruderhof Communities">Bruderhof</a> who were forced to leave England in 1941 because of their pacifist beliefs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[66]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[67]</a></sup> Many of these communities have retained their languages and culture, particularly the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Brazilian_people" title="Brazilian people">Brazilians</a>, who represent the largest and most prominent immigrant group, at around 400,000.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[68]</a></sup> Many Brazilian Paraguayans are of German, Italian and Polish descent.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[69]</a></sup> There are an estimated 63,000 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Afro-Paraguayans" title="Afro-Paraguayans">Afro-Paraguayans</a>, comprising 1% of the population.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[70]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Identifying_reliable_sources" title="Wikipedia:Identifying reliable sources"><span title="The material near this tag may rely on an unreliable source. (April 2014)">unreliable source?</span></a></i>]</sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Caacupe5.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="266" data-file-width="400" decoding="async" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Caacupe5.jpg/220px-Caacupe5.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Caacupe5.jpg/330px-Caacupe5.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/b/bb/Caacupe5.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Caacupe5.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A gathering in <a href="/wiki/Caacup%C3%A9" title="Caacup&#233;">Caacup&#233;</a></div></div></div>\n<p>There is no official data on the ethnic composition of the Paraguayan population, as the Department of Statistics, Surveys and Censuses<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[71]</a></sup> of Paraguay does not ask about <i>race</i> and <i>ethnicity</i> in census surveys, although it does inquire about the indigenous population. According to the census of 2002, the indigenous people made up 1.7% of Paraguay\'s total population.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[72]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Traditionally, the majority of the Paraguayan population is considered mixed (<i>mestizo</i> in Spanish). HLA-DRB1 polymorphism studies have shown the genetic distances between Paraguayans and Spanish populations were closer than between Paraguayans and Guaranis. Altogether these results suggest the predominance of the Spanish genetic in the Paraguayan population.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[73]</a></sup>\nAccording to the 2017 revision of the World Population Prospects<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UN_WPP_66-1"><a href="#cite_note-UN_WPP-66">[64]</a></sup>, Paraguay has a population of 6,725,308, 95% of which are Mestizo or white and 5% are labelled as "other", which includes members of indigenous tribal groups. They are divided into 17 distinct ethnolinguistic groupings, many of which are poorly documented.\nParaguay has one of the most prominent <a href="/wiki/Germans_in_Paraguay" title="Germans in Paraguay">German</a> communities in South America, with some 25,000 German-speaking <a href="/wiki/Mennonites_in_Paraguay" title="Mennonites in Paraguay">Mennonites</a> living in the Paraguayan <a href="/wiki/Gran_Chaco" title="Gran Chaco">Chaco</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[74]</a></sup> German settlers founded several towns as <a href="/wiki/Hohenau,_Paraguay" title="Hohenau, Paraguay">Hohenau</a>, <a href="/wiki/Filadelfia" title="Filadelfia">Filadelfia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Neuland_Colony" title="Neuland Colony">Neuland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Obligado" title="Obligado">Obligado</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nueva_Germania" title="Nueva Germania">Nueva Germania</a>. Several websites that promote German immigration to Paraguay claim that 5&#8211;7% of the population is of German ancestry,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Accuracy_dispute#Disputed_statement" title="Wikipedia:Accuracy dispute"><span title="The material near this tag is possibly inaccurate or nonfactual. (April 2014)">dubious</span></a> <span class="metadata"> &#8211; <a href="/wiki/Talk:Paraguay#Dubious" title="Talk:Paraguay">discuss</a></span></i>]</sup> including 150,000 people of German-Brazilian descent.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template noprint noexcerpt Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wikipedia:NOTRS" title="Wikipedia:NOTRS"><span title="Citations are from many German immigration promotion websites, there must be more objective sources for this (April 2014)">better&#160;source&#160;needed</span></a></i>]</sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[75]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[76]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[77]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[78]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[79]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Paraguay&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Paraguay" title="Religion in Paraguay">Religion in Paraguay</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Concepci%C3%B3n_Catholic_chapel.jpeg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1600" data-file-width="1200" decoding="async" height="227" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Concepci%C3%B3n_Catholic_chapel.jpeg/170px-Concepci%C3%B3n_Catholic_chapel.jpeg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Concepci%C3%B3n_Catholic_chapel.jpeg/255px-Concepci%C3%B3n_Catholic_chapel.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Concepci%C3%B3n_Catholic_chapel.jpeg/340px-Concepci%C3%B3n_Catholic_chapel.jpeg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Concepci%C3%B3n_Catholic_chapel.jpeg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Main Catholic Chapel in <a href="/wiki/Concepci%C3%B3n,_Paraguay" title="Concepci&#243;n, Paraguay">Concepci&#243;n, Paraguay</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Christianity, particularly <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_Catholicism" title="Roman Catholicism">Roman Catholicism</a>, is the dominant religion in Paraguay.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[80]</a></sup> According to the 2002 census, 89.9% of the population is Catholic, 6.2% is <a href="/wiki/Evangelicalism" title="Evangelicalism">Evangelical Protestant</a>, 1.1% identify with other Christian sects, and 0.6% practice indigenous religions. A U.S. State Department report on Religious Freedom names Roman Catholicism, evangelical Protestantism, mainline Protestantism, Judaism (Orthodox, Conservative, and Reform), <a href="/wiki/Mormonism" title="Mormonism">Mormonism</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_Faith" title="Bah&#225;\'&#237; Faith">Bah&#225;\'&#237; Faith</a> as prominent religious groups. It also mentions a large Muslim community in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alto_Paran%C3%A1" title="Alto Paran&#225;">Alto Paran&#225;</a> (as a result of Middle-Eastern immigration, especially from <a href="/wiki/Lebanon" title="Lebanon">Lebanon</a>) and a prominent Mennonite community in Boquer&#243;n.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-state1_83-0"><a href="#cite_note-state1-83">[81]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Paraguay&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Languages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Paraguay" title="Languages of Paraguay">Languages of Paraguay</a></div>\n<p>Paraguay is a bilingual nation. Both Spanish and Guaran&#237; are official languages. The Guarani language is a remarkable trace of the indigenous Guaran&#237; culture that has endured in Paraguay, which is generally understood by 95% of the population. Guaran&#237; claims its place as one of the last surviving and thriving of South American indigenous national languages. In 2015, Spanish was spoken by about 87% of the population, while Guaran&#237; is spoken by more than 90%, or slightly more than 5.8 million speakers. 52% of rural Paraguayans are bilingual in Guaran&#237;. While Guaran&#237; is still widely spoken, Spanish is generally given a preferential treatment in government, business, media and education as one of South America\'s <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lingua_francas" title="Lingua francas">lingua francas</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ethnologue-list_84-0"><a href="#cite_note-ethnologue-list-84">[82]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[83]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[84]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[85]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="barbox tleft" style="overflow-x: auto;">\n<div style="border:1px solid silver; font-size:88%; padding:0.4em; width:auto; background: white;">\n<table style="text-align:left; border-collapse:collapse; width:100%;">\n<tbody><tr style="background:#ddd"><th colspan="5" style="text-align:center;">Languages of Paraguay</th></tr>\n<tr style="text-align:right;">38,961\n</td></tr>\n</tbody></table>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Paraguay&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Paraguay" title="Music of Paraguay">Music of Paraguay</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cinema_of_Paraguay" title="Cinema of Paraguay">Cinema of Paraguay</a></div>\n<p>Paraguay\'s cultural heritage can be traced to the extensive <a href="/wiki/Interracial_marriage" title="Interracial marriage">intermarriage</a> between the original male Spanish settlers and indigenous <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Guarani_people" title="Guarani people">Guaran&#237;</a> women. Their culture is highly influenced by various European countries, including Spain. Therefore, Paraguayan culture is a fusion of two cultures and traditions; one European, the other, Southern Guaran&#237;. More than 93% of Paraguayans are <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mestizos" title="Mestizos">mestizos</a></i>, making Paraguay one of the most homogeneous countries in Latin America. A characteristic of this cultural fusion is the extensive bilingualism present to this day: more than 80% of Paraguayans speak both <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">Spanish</a> and the indigenous language, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Guaran%C3%AD_language" title="Guaran&#237; language">Guaran&#237;</a>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jopara" title="Jopara">Jopara</a>, a mixture of Guaran&#237; and Spanish, is also widely spoken.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ovecha_Ragu%C3%A9_Festival_Paraguay.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2640" data-file-width="3386" decoding="async" height="172" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Ovecha_Ragu%C3%A9_Festival_Paraguay.jpg/220px-Ovecha_Ragu%C3%A9_Festival_Paraguay.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Ovecha_Ragu%C3%A9_Festival_Paraguay.jpg/330px-Ovecha_Ragu%C3%A9_Festival_Paraguay.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Ovecha_Ragu%C3%A9_Festival_Paraguay.jpg/440px-Ovecha_Ragu%C3%A9_Festival_Paraguay.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ovecha_Ragu%C3%A9_Festival_Paraguay.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Ovecha Ragu&#233; Festival</div></div></div>\n<p>This cultural fusion is expressed in arts such as embroidery (<i>ao po\'&#237;</i>) and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nanduti" title="Nanduti">lace making</a> (<i>&#241;andut&#237;</i>). The <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Paraguay" title="Music of Paraguay">music of Paraguay</a>, which consists of lilting polkas, bouncy <i>galopas,</i> and languid <i><a href="/wiki/Guarania_(music)" title="Guarania (music)">guaranias</a></i> is played on the native harp. Paraguay\'s culinary heritage is also deeply influenced by this cultural fusion. Several popular dishes contain <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Manioc" title="Manioc">manioc</a>, a local staple crop similar to the <a href="/wiki/Cassava" title="Cassava">yuca</a> also known as Cassava root found in the <a href="/wiki/Southwestern_United_States" title="Southwestern United States">Southwestern United States</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico">Mexico</a>, as well as other indigenous ingredients. A popular dish is <i><a href="/wiki/Sopa_paraguaya" title="Sopa paraguaya">sopa paraguaya</a></i>, similar to a thick <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Corn_bread" title="Corn bread">corn bread</a>. Another notable food is <i><a href="/wiki/Chipa" title="Chipa">chipa</a></i>, a <a href="/wiki/Bagel" title="Bagel">bagel</a>-like bread made from <a href="/wiki/Cornmeal" title="Cornmeal">cornmeal</a>, manioc, and cheese. Many other dishes consist of different kinds of cheeses, onions, bell peppers, cottage cheese, cornmeal, milk, seasonings, butter, eggs and fresh corn kernels.\n</p><p>The 1950s and 1960s were the time of the flowering of a new generation of Paraguayan novelists and poets such as <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Ricardo_Maz%C3%B3" title="Jos&#233; Ricardo Maz&#243;">Jos&#233; Ricardo Maz&#243;</a>, <a href="/wiki/Roque_Vallejos" title="Roque Vallejos">Roque Vallejos</a>, and Nobel Prize nominee <a href="/wiki/Augusto_Roa_Bastos" title="Augusto Roa Bastos">Augusto Roa Bastos</a>. Several <a href="/wiki/Cinema_of_Paraguay" title="Cinema of Paraguay">Paraguayan films</a> have been made.\n</p><p>Inside the family, conservative values predominate. In lower classes, godparents have a special relationship to the family, since usually, they are chosen because of their favorable social position, in order to provide extra security for the children. Particular respect is owed them, in return for which the family can expect protection and patronage.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[87]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Paraguay&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sport_in_Paraguay" title="Sport in Paraguay">Sport in Paraguay</a></div>\n<p>Sport in Paraguay is an important part the country\'s national culture. <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">Football</a> is the most popular sport, and <a href="/wiki/Basketball" title="Basketball">basketball</a> is also very popular.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Paraguay_in_Pictures_90-0"><a href="#cite_note-Paraguay_in_Pictures-90">[88]</a></sup> Other sports such as <a href="/wiki/Volleyball" title="Volleyball">volleyball</a>, <a href="/wiki/Futsal" title="Futsal">futsal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Swimming_(sport)" title="Swimming (sport)">swimming</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tennis" title="Tennis">tennis</a> are also popular.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Paraguay_in_Pictures_90-1"><a href="#cite_note-Paraguay_in_Pictures-90">[88]</a></sup> Additional Paraguayan sports and pastimes include <a href="/wiki/Rugby_union" title="Rugby union">rugby union</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chess" title="Chess">chess</a>, <a href="/wiki/Motorsport" title="Motorsport">motorsport</a>, <a href="/wiki/Golf" title="Golf">golf</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rowing_(sport)" title="Rowing (sport)">rowing</a>.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Paraguay&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Paraguay" title="Education in Paraguay">Education in Paraguay</a></div>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_universities_in_Paraguay" title="List of universities in Paraguay">List of universities in Paraguay</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_schools_in_Paraguay" title="List of schools in Paraguay">List of schools in Paraguay</a></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Literacy" title="Literacy">Literacy</a> was about 93.6% and 87.7% of Paraguayans finish the 5th grade according to <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a>\'s last Educational Development Index 2008. Literacy does not differ much by gender.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hdrstats.undp.org_91-0"><a href="#cite_note-hdrstats.undp.org-91">[89]</a></sup> A more recent study<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-abc.com.py_63-1"><a href="#cite_note-abc.com.py-63">[61]</a></sup> reveals that attendance at primary school by children between 6 and 12 years old is about 98%. Primary education is free and mandatory and takes nine years. Secondary education takes three years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hdrstats.undp.org_91-1"><a href="#cite_note-hdrstats.undp.org-91">[89]</a></sup>\nMain universities in Paraguay include:\n</p>\n<ul><li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_University_of_Asunci%C3%B3n" title="National University of Asunci&#243;n">National University of Asunci&#243;n</a> (public and founded in 1889)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[90]</a></sup></li>\n<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Autonomous_University_of_Asunci%C3%B3n" title="Autonomous University of Asunci&#243;n">Autonomous University of Asunci&#243;n</a> (private and founded in 1979)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[91]</a></sup></li>\n<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Universidad_Cat%C3%B3lica_Nuestra_Se%C3%B1ora_de_la_Asunci%C3%B3n" title="Universidad Cat&#243;lica Nuestra Se&#241;ora de la Asunci&#243;n">Universidad Cat&#243;lica Nuestra Se&#241;ora de la Asunci&#243;n</a> (private and run by the church).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[92]</a></sup></li>\n<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Universidad_Americana" title="Universidad Americana">Universidad Americana</a> (private).</li>\n<li><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Universidad_del_Pac%C3%ADfico_(Paraguay)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Universidad del Pac&#237;fico (Paraguay) (page does not exist)">Universidad del Pac&#237;fico</a> (private and founded in 1991).</li></ul>\n<p>The net primary enrollment rate was at 88% in 2005.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hdrstats.undp.org_91-2"><a href="#cite_note-hdrstats.undp.org-91">[89]</a></sup> Public expenditure on education was about 4.3% of GDP in the early 2000s.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hdrstats.undp.org_91-3"><a href="#cite_note-hdrstats.undp.org-91">[89]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Health">Health</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Paraguay&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Health">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Health_in_Paraguay" title="Health in Paraguay">Health in Paraguay</a></div>\n<p>Average life expectancy in Paraguay is rather high given its poverty: as of  2006<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Paraguay&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, it was 75 years,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[93]</a></sup> equivalent to far wealthier Argentina, and the 8th highest in the Americas according to World Health Organization. Public expenditure on health is 2.6% of GDP, while private health expenditure is 5.1%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hdrstats.undp.org_91-4"><a href="#cite_note-hdrstats.undp.org-91">[89]</a></sup> Infant mortality was 20 per 1,000 births in 2005.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hdrstats.undp.org_91-5"><a href="#cite_note-hdrstats.undp.org-91">[89]</a></sup> Maternal mortality was 150 per 100,000 live births in 2000.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hdrstats.undp.org_91-6"><a href="#cite_note-hdrstats.undp.org-91">[89]</a></sup>\nThe <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank</a> has helped the Paraguayan government reduce the country\'s maternal and infant mortality. The <i>Mother and Child Basic Health Insurance Project</i> aimed to contribute to reducing mortality by increasing the use of selected life-saving services included in the country\'s Mother and Child Basic Health Insurance Program (MCBI) by women of child-bearing age, and children under age six in selected areas. To this end, the project also targeted improving the quality and efficiency of the health service network within certain areas, in addition to increasing the Ministry of Public Health and Social Welfare\'s (MSPBS) management.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[94]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Paraguay&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div aria-label="Portals" class="noprint portal plainlist tright" role="navigation" style="margin:0.5em 0 0.5em 1em;border:solid #aaa 1px">\n<ul Paraguay">Outline of Paraguay</a></li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a See the classic book of the Blanco Leader Luis Alberto de Herrera (1927): "El Drama del 65 - La Culpa Mitrista", pp. 11 - 33. Bareiro y Ramos Editors. Montevideo, Uruguay</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-29"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-29">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Sir Richard Francis Burton: "Letters from the Battlefields of Paraguay", p.76 &#8211; Tinsley Brothers Editors &#8211; London (1870) &#8211; Burton, as a witness of the conflict, marks this date (12&#8211;16 October 1864) as the real beginning of the war. He writes (and it\'s the most logic account, considering the facts): <i>The Brazilian Army invades the Banda Oriental, despite the protestations of President L&#243;pez, who declared that such invasion would be held a "casus belli"</i>.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-30"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-30">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Pomer, Le&#243;n (2008): "La Guerra del Paraguay: Estado, Pol&#237;tica y Negocios" (in Spanish), pp. 240 - 241. Buenos Aires: Editorial Colihue.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-31"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-31">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Hooker, T.D., 2008, "The Paraguayan War". Nottingham: Foundry Books, pp. 105&#8211;108. <link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r879151008" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">ISBN</a>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/1901543153" title="Special:BookSources/1901543153">1901543153</a></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-32"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-32">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The classical view asserts that Francisco Solano L&#243;pez\'s expansionist and hegemonic views are the main reason for the outbreak of the conflict. The traditional Paraguayan view, held by the "<i>lopistas</i>" (supporters of Solano L&#243;pez, both in Paraguay and worldwide), affirms that Paraguay acted in self-defense and for the protection of the "Equilibrium of the Plate Basin". This view is usually contested by the "<i>anti-lopistas</i>" (also known in Paraguay as "<i>legionarios</i>"), who favoured the "<i>Triple Alliance</i>". Revisionist views, both from right and left wing national-populists, put a great emphasis on the influence of the British Empire in the conflict, a view that is discarded by a majority of historians.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-33"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-33">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation book">Rubinsein, W. D. (2004). <a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=nMMAk4VwLLwC" rel="nofollow"><i>Genocide: a history</i></a>. Pearson Education. p.&#160;94. <a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">ISBN</a>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0-582-50601-8" title="Special:BookSources/0-582-50601-8">0-582-50601-8</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Genocide%3A+a+history&amp;rft.pages=94&amp;rft.pub=Pearson+Education&amp;rft.date=2004&amp;rft.isbn=0-582-50601-8&amp;rft.aulast=Rubinsein&amp;rft.aufirst=W.+D.&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3DnMMAk4VwLLwC&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AParaguay"></span><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r879151008" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-34"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-34">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Hip&#243;lito Sanchez Quell: "Los 50.000 Documentos Paraguayos Llevados al Brasil".
